- **Message-ID:** `<8a61d4cc-55e9-437d-8926-6f385b8e7d0e@y11g2000yqm.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<098a698a-a3da-4e55-b6b5-12a58ee646f9@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <f676deda-3d7e-4157-95ca-d74902256a2c@5g2000yqz.googlegroups.com> <8cv9ahFa0uU1@mid.individual.net> <0848dc74-354f-431c-b4c6-f0b97daf8e07@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Sep 1, 9:20 am, Derek Schrock <derekschr...@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> So the idea here is to find all instances of "string" plus the
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
> - Show quoted text -

I've thought along similar lines. The CoBOL program already has line
numbers, so don't need the -n. It's been a few years since I wrote
some awk, so I'll have to refresh my memory a bit. But the strategy
should be fairly simple. For my purposes, the "context" need only be
the preceding five lines or so. (Also keep in mind that I need this
"context" _only_ for those lines that contain the target data-element
on a line all by itself, without a preceding "TO" on that same line,
because I can grep those lines already and have all the info I need.)

So use an array of size 5 say, and accumulate the "context" as I scan
the file, keeping only the five most recent line. Then look for the
regexp that matches an "isolated data-element" and print out the
preceding five lines and the current line.

As I said, my awk is rusty, but it would go something like this...

BEGIN {
       context[1]=""
       context[2]=""
       context[3]=""
       context[4]=""
       context[5]=""
      }
/^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? */ {print
"~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~"
            print context[1]
            print context[2]
            print context[3]
            print context[4]
            print context[5]
            print $0
           }
/./        {context[1]=context[2]
            context[2]=context[3]
            context[3]=context[4]
            context[4]=context[5]
            context[5]=$0
           }
END   {
       print "Done!"
      }

... which produces the result -

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
002200
00220003
002300 A-100-CLEAR-XFER-
FIELDS.                                         00230000
002400     MOVE SPACES TO XFER-GENERIC-SEGMENT-
KEYS,                    00240000
002500                    XFER-AFDC-ACCT-
ID,                            00250000
002600                    XFER-AFDC-
CASE,                               00260003
002700                    XFER-BLK-BOX-
ACCOUNT                          00270005
Done!

And I can immediately see, that yes, this is an occurrence where XFER-
BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT is a destination for a MOVE.

This brings me full circle to the original question, which is - is the
regexp /^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? */ for "XFER-BLK-BOX-
ACCOUNT alone on a line" optimally correct?

Ken
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: grep'ing CoBOL source

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** Derek Schrock <derekschrock@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-02T06:38:51-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<09fa73c7-aa30-47e6-b7ba-bb2b4accd8ef@v41g2000yqv.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<098a698a-a3da-4e55-b6b5-12a58ee646f9@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <f676deda-3d7e-4157-95ca-d74902256a2c@5g2000yqz.googlegroups.com> <8cv9ahFa0uU1@mid.individual.net> <0848dc74-354f-431c-b4c6-f0b97daf8e07@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <8a61d4cc-55e9-437d-8926-6f385b8e7d0e@y11g2000yqm.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Sep 1, 11:49 am, Ken <klsha...@att.net> wrote:
> On Sep 1, 9:20 am, Derek Schrock <derekschr...@gmail.com> wrote:
>
…[89 more quoted lines elided]…
> Ken

The awk looks fine but the /./ isn't really needed:

awk '
{  #This action set will run on everyline
  #do something
}'

is the same as

awk '
/./ { #If the line has anything on it, every line has a '\n'
  #do something
}'

half dozen, six in the other...

I would have used grep's -n line number, awk's NF, and a larger buffer
once you found a match and read the buffer backwards until you match a
verb (MOVE, etc....).


As far as the regex goes it may match lines that you're not expecting:

/^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? */

Match conditions:
"^......" Line begins with any thing for the first six characters
#cobol lin num
" *" followed by any number of spaces
",?" followed by an optional comma
" *" followed by any number of spaces
"XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT" followed by the string "XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT"
" *" followed by any number of spaces
",?" followed by an optional comma
" *" followed by any number of spaces  #Here lies the issue


So the following lines for example:

123456          , XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT ,
....
164325         XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT
.....
654321         ,XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT  MORETEXTAFTER  #We don't want to
match this right?

If so the regex would change to require a read to the end of line:

/^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? *$/

Adding the '$' forces the read to the end of line changing the last
condition from the above list:

" *$" followed by any number of spaces to the end of line.  #Added for
"alone on a line"

There could be additional optimizations to the regex but I if it works
it works.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: grep'ing CoBOL source

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** Ken <klshafer@att.net>
- **Date:** 2010-09-02T09:01:22-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<11cf1607-ee2e-4fd0-9b75-deca07dc5389@x25g2000yqj.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<098a698a-a3da-4e55-b6b5-12a58ee646f9@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <f676deda-3d7e-4157-95ca-d74902256a2c@5g2000yqz.googlegroups.com> <8cv9ahFa0uU1@mid.individual.net> <0848dc74-354f-431c-b4c6-f0b97daf8e07@d8g2000yqf.googlegroups.com> <8a61d4cc-55e9-437d-8926-6f385b8e7d0e@y11g2000yqm.googlegroups.com> <09fa73c7-aa30-47e6-b7ba-bb2b4accd8ef@v41g2000yqv.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Sep 2, 9:38 am, Derek Schrock <derekschr...@gmail.com> wrote:
> On Sep 1, 11:49 am, Ken <klsha...@att.net> wrote:
>
>
> The awk looks fine but the /./ isn't really needed:

Yeah, I figured that out later :-) - an example of something I knew
once, but had since forgot (my last awk programming was about 10 years
ago. I'm picking it up again...  hmmmmm.... later reading of the awk
man page shows me that "you do not need to declare awk variables and
you do not need to initialize them. The value of an unitialized
variable is the empty string..." - so I guess the BEGIN assignments
are also unneeded.
>
/>
> I would have used grep's -n line number, awk's NF, and a larger buffer
> once you found a match and read the buffer backwards until you match a
> verb (MOVE, etc....).

That's a good idea. What we're really doing then is scanning backwards
until we hit the beginning of the CoBOL "statement" (the verb),
instead of just an arbitrary number of lines.

>
> As far as the regex goes it may match lines that you're not expecting:
>
> /^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? */

Very true, in fact I tweaked the awk below to delete some of those
undesired lines...

>
> Match conditions:
> "^......" Line begins with any thing for the first six characters

It's usually a 6-digit line number, but sometimes it is spaces. I
guess I could use the [ 0-9] syntax. But again, I was kinda lazy. dot
(.) worked just fine :-).

> #cobol lin num
> " *" followed by any number of spaces
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> "alone on a line"

Yes, you are touching on some stuff I encountered. In fact, in another
iteration I had experimented with -
"^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *[,.]* *[0-9]*$"

(where I had the trailing [0-9] because there are also line numbers in
73-80)

However, in considering...
> 654321         ,XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT  MORETEXTAFTER  #We don't want to
> match this right?
I did want to show up the following:
123456           ,XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT, SOME-OTHR-DATA-ELT,
12345678

so that's why I backed off from trying to match all the way to the end-
of-line $.

>
> There could be additional optimizations to the regex but I if it works
> it works.-

That's what I really, really like about grep and awk. Can tinker to my
heart's delight with nearly instantaneous feedback and fine-tune to
focus in on what I am looking for.

My latest versions - wrap in a tiny shell script, and do some glob'ing
on *.cpy...

context.ksh:
echo "Running awk to scan for isolated XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT, -ACCT-NUM
lines..."
awk -f context.awk *.cpy >context.txt
echo "context.txt contains the isolated lines in context."
echo "Done!"

Then modify the awk script to delete the unnecessary BEGIN section,
look for both XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT and redefined alias XFER-BLK-BOX-
ACCT-NUM, and print out the file name that contains the hit (now
necessary because we are glob'ing). Add a couple tweaks to suppress
false hits like PIC lines in Working-Storage and <, >, + comparisons,
so the following works pretty well:

context.awk:
/^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCOUNT *,? */ {
            hits = match($0,/ PIC /) + match($0,/[<>=]/)
            if (hits == 0) {
                print
"~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~"
                print FILENAME, ":", context[1]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[2]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[3]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[4]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[5]
                print FILENAME, ":", $0
                }
           }
/^...... *,? *XFER-BLK-BOX-ACCT-NUM *,? */ {
            hits = match($0,/ PIC /) + match($0,/[<>=]/)
            if (hits == 0) {
                print
"~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~"
                print FILENAME, ":", context[1]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[2]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[3]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[4]
                print FILENAME, ":", context[5]
                print FILENAME, ":", $0
                }
           }
           {context[1]=context[2]
            context[2]=context[3]
            context[3]=context[4]
            context[4]=context[5]
            context[5]=$0
           }

Thanks for you feedback.

Ken
```

```
>So the idea here is to find all instances of "string" plus the
>context?

>If so you could use grep's -n (assuming you have that option).  This
>will print the line number along with the matched line.  Using this
>information you could write a complementary awk program to pull the
>context.

The SD Source Code Search engine will let you code various searches
in terms of (COBOL) langauge elements rather than characters.

Specifically for the issue
discussed here, you can tell it to capture K lines of context;
the search log file will then contain the the actual hits and K lines
before and after the hit.   No messing with awk needed.
www.semanticdesigns.com/Products/SearchEngine
```

## Thread: OT: NZ earthquake — 16 msgs

_Topics: [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: NZ earthquake

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-09-04T12:39:52+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8ediqrFokqU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
The city of Christchurch (NZ) was hit by an earthquake which measured 7.5 on 
the Richter scale, at 4:35 am this morning (Saturday 4th, local time)

I had some private mail from people who post to CLC, asking if I was OK. 
Most of the country (apart from Christchurch) is fine and I understand 
things are getting back to normal in Christchurch with a massive clear up 
being undertaken.

Christchurch is a major South Island city and the South Island of NZ is 
generally sparsely populated, apart from Christchurch and Dunedin, the two 
major cities, and a sprinkling of larger towns. Most of the time earthquakes 
occur in unoccupied areas, but occasionally we get a town being hit. It is 
very unusual for a major city to be hit by such a devastating shock and if I 
had to guess which city would be, I would've guessed Wellington as more 
likely because there is a fault line that runs right through it.

Both major islands are subject to earthquakes (there are around 15,000 
recorded every year) of which around 100 can be felt. However, the North 
Island is much more densely populated, so earthquakes there are far more 
likely to hit population centres.When I was growing up in Wellington they 
were a fairly usual occurrence and I remember one that knocked chess pieces 
off the board as we were playng at school. Mostly, there is just a tremor, 
like a heavy truck going past and no-one really pays much attention to them. 
It has been a couple of years since I felt anything here in Tauranga (North 
Island, Bay of Plenty), and that was a tremor which vibrated the house for 
about 20 seconds. My neighbour phoned to see if I had felt it and we agreed 
it wasn't a passing truck :-). The last serious one I expereinced in 
Tauranga was around 30 years ago when I was home for a visit. That one 
cracked my concrete driveway but did no damage to the house itself or the 
contents.It was centred 20 KMs off shore out in the Bay and did cause a mild 
tsunami.

The point is that earthquakes generally are not problematic for us due to 
sparse population density, being taught defence drills from the time we are 
little, and all modern buildings being earthquake resistant. I understand 
there have been no reports of death or serious injury despite the extensive 
property damage in Christchurch. All high rise buildings in cities like 
Auckland and the major centres have been subject to an earthquake code for 
over 75 years now (there was a serious review of the codes in 1931 after the 
devastating Napier earthquake which killed and injured hundreds of people), 
and NZ is one of the leading researchers into the effect of earthquakes on 
buildings.Although it is probably impossible to build an earthquake proof 
building, it is certainly possible to build structures that can withstand 
high degrees of shock.

Nevertheless, it is a timely reminder that we can't get away with it 
indefinitely and sooner or later there will be hits in major cities.

This site answers most questions about the nature of earthquakes: 
http://www.gns.cri.nz/what/earthact/earthquakes/earthquakefaq.html#1

My thanks to all who expressed their concern

Pete.
```

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> The city of Christchurch (NZ) was hit by an earthquake which measured
> 7.5 on the Richter scale, at 4:35 am this morning (Saturday 4th,
> local time)

The extent of the damage is now much clearer.

Although property damage will be a couple of billion dollars, the major 
factor emerging is the effect that events like this have on the population.

The human damage is much more than the property damage. It is quite moving 
to see families and children trying to come to terms with the upheaval in 
their lives. Times like this bring out the best (and occasionally), the 
worst in us. There were isolated reports of looting but this is now stopped 
as police and army have poured in to the area.The outpouring of support and 
practical help has been incredible both from the local community and the 
country at large. We are a relatively small family here. (4 million).

Continuing aftershocks (some of which would be considered major earthquakes 
in their own right) are problematic at the moment and hindering attempts to 
clean up and get people rehoused.

People interested in engineering may find this report of interest: 
http://www.sunlive.co.nz/17450a1.page

Pete.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: OT: NZ earthquake

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-09-08T23:15:06+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8ep9hsFnj3U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<8ediqrFokqU1@mid.individual.net> <84kc86h9uhj9jbd2opm99t54bv5018ug2o@4ax.com>`

```
Howard Brazee wrote:
> On Sat, 4 Sep 2010 12:39:52 +1200, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> OK.

Thanks Howard, I really appreciate the thought.

There was another earthquake yesterday on the East Coast of the North Island 
about 150 miles from where I live.  (Christchurch is around  450 miles). 
Fortunately this one was in a sparsely populated area and resulted in very 
little damage and no injury or loss of life.

Sadly, there were some serious aftershocks again today in Christchurch, 
which have really hampered restoration. These "aftershocks" are over 5 on 
the Richter scale and would be considered "earthquakes" in most places.The 
Government has come out and made a statement that aftershocks will be 
considered "earthquakes" for the purposes of insurance and compensation. 
This is a relief to many families who thought they may get no compensation 
on the technicality that their house was damaged by an "aftershock" and not 
an "earthquake".

Whatever your politics, you have to admire the Prime Minister, who cancelled 
a trip to U.K. and has been in the quake zone assessing damage and talking 
to people. He has made himself available on TV and in person to answer 
questions  (very directly and honestly) and provide help and support to 
anxious people.  I didn't vote for him or his party, but I've been very 
impressed by his leadership and concern through this. Latest assessments 
place the damage repair at between 2 and 4 billion dollars. (Remember, we 
have a population of 4 million...)

As a nation we are reeling from the ongoing effects of this (it has been 5 
days now of continual aftershocks that make it almost impossible to continue 
cleanup; it is all we can do to ensure housing, water, sewage and 
electricity for the homeless).

It is absolutely heartbreaking to see the carnage here and the toll in human 
terms. Although no-one has died (and we are all thankful for that) lives 
have been destroyed by this.

All of us are doing whatever we can to help Christchurch, but it is very 
difficult when the situation is so unstable. Today's shocks destroyed some 
of the work already done. People on the spot are facing nights of 
uncertainty and anxiety. It is particularly hard for the kids. Schools are 
closed in the area and some that would have re-opened tomorrow, now won't 
because of the aftershocks.

Given the other earthquake yesterday in the North Island, it looks as if the 
whole plate is in a state of motion and we really have no idea what will 
happen next. The best we can hope for is stability, and a chance to clean up 
the mess.

Hopefully, once things settle down, it should be quite some time before we 
experience more of this.

On a more positive note, a huge amount of invaluable data is being gained 
and experts from all over the world are flying in to view and study the 
cause and effects. I was amused to see a couple of American Geologists 
almost ecstatic at how "perfect" this quake was and really getting excited 
about the knowledge it would provide and the light it would shed for 
"earthquake science" in the future.

Aerial photographs reveal a 32 KM rift along an ancient fault that no one 
even knew existed. Best guess as to the last time this fault ruptured are 
between 6000 and 8000 years ago. All visible surface signs of it have been 
obliterated so farms and suburbs were built on it, in blissful ignorance 
that it might tear again. Modern science is going to provide us ways to 
detect these ancient faults, and this earthquake is providing some of the 
data which will go towards doing that.

It is indeed an ill wind which blows nobody any good...

Pete.
```

```
Howard Brazee wrote:

All good wishes for your operation, Howard. If it is any consolation, I have 
a friend here who is diabetic and has 6 stents inserted in various arteries. 
He injects himself with insulin twice a day and you'd think his life must be 
miserable. On the contrary, he is one of the most cheerful people I know and 
he doesn't let his condition affect his lifestyle in any way. He enjoys good 
wine, is highly active in musical and dramatic societies, and even assists 
others who are less capable than he. It is an inspiration sometimes to see 
heow people cope with adversity.

I attended the funeral of one of my closest friends yesterday and was asked 
to write a poem for her. (She died suddenly last Friday and I have been 
pretty devasted in the ensuing period.) But she had asked that I write 
something for her and read it at her funeral and the family were expecting 
me to. I couldn't even think about it without dissolving into tears and 
began to despair that I could have anything ready by Wednesday. But she was 
a wise lady.  She knew I couldn't let her down, and she also knew that the 
exercise of doing this would help me come to terms with the loss. It 
certainly did and although I still feel sad and shocked over her going, I am 
coping with it now.

I know it is a platitude, but there is definitely value in the idea that 
facing up to things makes us stronger.

I hope you have a speedy recovery and are back on the golf course before 
anyone knows you are gone :-)

Pete.
```

```
On Sep 5, 7:11 am, Lüko Willms <lueko.wil...@domain.invalid> wrote:
> Am 05.09.2010 00:37, schrieb Richard:
>
…[20 more quoted lines elided]…
> L.W.

At the risk of having nits picked:

OSX is a variant of Unix running on Apple platforms. Windows is
Microsoft's operating system for Intel and AMD chipped platforms
(often referred to as WINTEL). The chip instruction sets are very
different (correct me if I am wrong people) and are proprietory to the
platforms. Also, memory addresses on Apple chipsets will not be
analogous to those on Wintel chipsets. So, the programs from Windows
platforms will not run on OSX platforms although OSX code can run on
Windows platforms with the right emulators.

It is a bit like trying to run ICL code on an IBM platform - all wrong.
```

```
On Sep 5, 11:14 pm, Alistair <alist...@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote:
> On Sep 5, 7:11 am, Lüko Willms <lueko.wil...@domain.invalid> wrote:
>
…[37 more quoted lines elided]…
> It is a bit like trying to run ICL code on an IBM platform - all wrong.

Apple Mac desktops and server were originally Motorola 680x0, they
switched to IBM's POWERPC, then to Intel x86. The iPhone and iPod,
which also run a variety of OSX, use ARM processors.

OpenCOBOL can be compiled to various platforms. It runs under Cygwin,
a Unix like environment for Windows; native Windows; Linux; and on
OSX. It compiles and runs on ARM processors and probably other
processor families.

The issue, as explained, is that there is no pre-built install for
Macs.

So, no, it is nothing like your analogy.
```

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** Lüko Willms <lueko.willms@domain.invalid>
- **Date:** 2010-09-04T16:12:07+02:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4c825380$0$6274$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<07b2b109-2289-4f10-8e32-03aabb3755f6@g17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<0c65f6d9-b98b-4be5-892e-0642a5a5cc17@x21g2000yqa.googlegroups.com> <i50o2p$qus$1@reader1.panix.com> <593c7c77-cd52-4a76-ba31-7ac6925e8145@v41g2000yqv.googlegroups.com> <07b2b109-2289-4f10-8e32-03aabb3755f6@g17g2000yqe.googlegroups.com>`

```
Am 24.08.2010 22:01, schrieb Alistair:


>> >  Not sure if I can have a main cursor and
>> >  join the other two tables or try and join the first 2 in the main and
>> >  then read the 3rd table. Trying to avoid tabling them all up and doing
>> >  search alls- Hide quoted text -

> Go for the big hit. Do all three in one join.

   Right on! DECLARE a CURSOR with all the fields which you need from 
the three tables, JOINt by the common key fields and have it sorted by 
the main key. Then you can process it like a simple sequential file, a 
job COBOL is great for.


Cheers,
L.W.
```

```
Not sure if anyone is interested but here is an announcement number for
a COBOL job with the Navy at King's Bay, GA.

SE0-2210-11-MZ781737-DEer 

Just enter it into the search box on USAJOBS.

for someone to recode the application in Java when no one responds to the
first set of ads.

bill
```

```
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>reference to some person's name so I looked it up on-line.

It was named for the King family. A more complete history of Kingsland
GA  is at:
http://www.kingslandgeorgia.com/index.aspx?nid=106

However, Old Kings Road, which began at nearly Colerain GA and ran
down the Atlantic coast to New Smyrna FL, WAS named for the king of
England. It is still a prominant road in Palm Coast. We cannot rename
it President's Road because there is already a street bearing that
name in Orlando. We cannot use a Democratic name in Florida. Bush,
Cheney, Reagan, Eisenhower and Nixon are taken. In fact, EVERY
Republican president back to Lincoln is in use, mostly in
Jacksonville. Even Tiger Woods is taken. What are we to do?
http://www.emporia.edu/earthsci/student/lowe2/old_king_road.htm
```

```
 - both 9's
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Test request

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-06T13:26:34-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Dnaho.139519$De6.79400@en-nntp-01.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<jHAgo.95193$Qg.29047@en-nntp-04.dc1.easynews.com> <4c84ea0d$0$50442$14726298@news.sunsite.dk> <qd6a86h4k7m59j5566pobc1tb7jkjgphcq@4ax.com>`

```
"SkippyPB" <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com> wrote in message 
news:qd6a86h4k7m59j5566pobc1tb7jkjgphcq@4ax.com...
> On Mon, 06 Sep 2010 15:18:05 +0200, Fred Mobach <fred@mobach.nl>
> wrote:
<snip>
> OK, I'm confused.  Looking at the source and looking at the results it
> appears that TABL1 in sub program Cont1 did not "honor" the Move 5 to
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> -- 
Thanks for looking at the source code.  You are corectly identifiying WHY I 
created these tests - and I am (sort-of) glad that all the tests are coming 
out the same.

Yes, Virginia (to borrow from another thread),
  the LOCAL item is being ignored in teh nested program.

I have been working with PL22.4 (previously J4) on a question that 
originated with Report Writer - Source and Sum clauses and 
Accept/Display/Screen Section - FROM, TO, and USING clauses.  It turns out 
that this is a general GLOBAL/local issue.

What it appears that the Standard requires ('85 and '02) and that 
implementors all did this correctly, is that

- When there is an explicit reference to a data item (normally in the 
Procedure Division, but this ALSO can be in a data or environment division 
statement, such as Occurs Dependin on,  FROM, SUM,  CURSOR IS, RELATIVE KEY 
is, etc0, that the rules for name "scoping" occur, i.e. you look for a local 
name that matches and if you don't find one you go up the chain of 
containing program to find a GLOBAL item that matches.

HOWEVER, when there is an implicit reference to an item, such as a reference 
to a group item with the GLOBAL attribute and taht group contains an ODO, 
then it is the "originally identified in the original data division" item 
that is used, and NOT any local item with the same name.

This is (or may be) a "little surprising" but it turns out there are rules 
to support this and (happily) all compilers tested seem to work this way.

In some (not all) cases, there are rules that state that if the "group-type" 
item is GLOBAL that the "referenced" item must also be global.  (This is 
true for Occurs Depending ON), but in some cases such rules do not exist and 
the implicitly referenced item may be used in an "implicit reference" (in a 
contained program) but the same item may not be referenced in an explicit 
statement in that same nested program.  This is "weird but true"
```

---

<a id="t-afd5d20115"></a>
## Thread: How to avoid bad gigs — 10 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### How to avoid bad gigs

- **From:** Robert Wagner <no@email.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-05T00:47:46-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com>`

```
I recently retired after 12 years of contract programming in 
Cobol, C and SQL on Unix. Out of 16 contracts, 6 were bad and 
10 were good. In retrospect, I realize there is a 
criterion that would have rejected all 6 bad jobs while 
not rejecting (false positive) any of the 10 good ones. 

Here is a way to assess the employment tone of a city, using data from
a single source: 
http://www.bea.gov/newsreleases/regional/lapi/mpi_newsrelease.htm
Using C = Percent change 2004-2005 and I = Per capita personal income,
the formula is ROUND(((1+(C/100))^6) * (I/1000)), which approximates
income six years hence.
Passing score is 49 (,000)

Results:         
  Bad gigs
Greensboro NC     40 
Pittsburgh PA     46 
Bentonville AR    40 
St Louis MO       47 
Champaign IL      28 
Akron OH          42 
  Good gigs
Chicago IL        49   twice
Jacksonville FL   49 
Albany NY         43   (C was higher when I was there in 2000)
NYC-NJ            62   twice
Minneapolis MN    53 
Houston TX        62 
Orlando FL        53 

Highest scores go to Bridgeport CT, Washington DC, San Francisco CA, 
San Jose CA, Boulder CO, Trenton NJ, Boston MA, Houston TX and NYC.
Lowest scores (omitting Gulf Coast) go to Pine Bluff AR, Flint MI,
Yakima WA, Merced CA, Danville IL, Saginaw MI, Canton OH and Champaign
IL.
Large cities with failing scores are Milwaukee WI, Kansas City MO, 
Indianapolis IN, Providence RI, Cincinnati OH, Columbus OH, Seattle
WA, Detroit MI, Cleveland OH, Riverside CA, Buffalo NY and Rochester
NY.

The formula is measuring locals' belief other jobs are available.  
An employee puts up with a lot of abuse if (s)he believes, rightly
or wrongly, losing the job means selling the house and moving.
Companies in such places devolve to a management style based on fear
rather than accomplishment, a self-reinforcing dynamic that is a sure
path to eventual failure. 

Note the criterion is not specific to the IT industry.
```

#### ↳ Re: How to avoid bad gigs

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2010-09-07T12:43:44+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<i65c20$ge9$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com>`

```
>Cobol, C and SQL on Unix. Out of 16 contracts, 6 were bad and

An interesting theorem, Mr Wagner, and one that's easily back-tested by 
finding the appropriate date for the year in which you had your contract 
in a given area and seeing if the Bureau of Economic Analysis data six 
years' prior generates the same conclusion.

>Highest scores go to Bridgeport CT, Washington DC, San Francisco CA, 
>San Jose CA, Boulder CO, Trenton NJ, Boston MA, Houston TX and NYC.

Mr Wagner, this is puzzling.  Bridgeport, CT is one of the most miserable 
US cities with which I'm familiar and it ranks so highly?  This might be 
due to the 'Bill Gates Walks Into A Bar' syndrome, as Bridgeport is lumped 
in with the Stamford and Norwalk areas; I recall hearing that Stamford 
used to have more Fortune 500 company headquarters than Manhattan and 
(along with Norwalk) serves as a commuting-point for Manhattan... one 
should be very, *very* careful with these numbers.

[snip]

>The formula is measuring locals' belief other jobs are available.  
>An employee puts up with a lot of abuse if (s)he believes, rightly
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>path to eventual failure. 

Long ago I learned to respond to 'Hey, we gave you a job, didn't we?' with 
'No, you believed that you could make a sufficient profit from my work' 
and 'You're lucky you even *have* a job here' with 'No, *you're* lucky I 
have chosen to work with you...

... and long ago I learned that I am a moderately decent consultant and a 
very, *very* bad employee.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: How to avoid bad gigs

- **From:** Robert Wagner <no@email.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-08T01:40:06-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<uo1e86dacc29t76bneqtcdiljcvvm7msqh@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com> <i65c20$ge9$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
On Tue, 7 Sep 2010 12:43:44 +0000 (UTC), docdwarf@panix.com () wrote:

>In article <fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com>,
>Robert Wagner  <no@email.com> wrote:
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>years' prior generates the same conclusion.

Generally, the numbers don't change much from year to year. Champaign
IL looks unusually bad because a GM plant had closed the year before. 

>>Highest scores go to Bridgeport CT, Washington DC, San Francisco CA, 
>>San Jose CA, Boulder CO, Trenton NJ, Boston MA, Houston TX and NYC.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
>should be very, *very* careful with these numbers.

Bridgeport reflects NYC's statistics since most of its income is
earned there. 

Headquarters by city is found at:
http://money.cnn.com/magazines/fortune/fortune500/2007/cities/
It is interesting to note Houston is second place, after NYC. 

At one time, NYC had 40% of F-500 headquarters. Now it has less than
10%.

>>The formula is measuring locals' belief other jobs are available.  
>>An employee puts up with a lot of abuse if (s)he believes, rightly
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>very, *very* bad employee.

My point is management style reflects independence or desperation of
employees. Then contractors are treated the same way, in spite of the
fact they are not locals. Thus, assessment criteria for contracting
should be the same as for employment. 

I find it interesting that extrapolated per capita income falls in a
fairly narrow range -- 49 - 62K -- contradicting the notion of low
cost of living in flyover states. Like other commodities, prices of
labor and housing are determined by supply and demand.
```

```
>who was correct.

I GUESSED Bridgeport is an economic satellite of NYC, but I did not
guess at statistics showing it to be the best place to work in the US.

My algorithm finds good places to work, not necessarily good places to
live or vacation, although there is a high correlation. One of the
highest rated small cities is Casper WY. I find it hard to believe
anywhere in WY is a fun place to live. 

>>>>My point is management style reflects independence or desperation of
>>>>employees.
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>'underwater mortgage' this may no longer be the case.

An outsourced gig should be assessed using management's home city, not
the work city. I omitted one of my gigs in Montgomery AL (a reject)
because management was in Washington DC (a good place). 

Places with many underwater mortages will not score well because they
have low or negative growth. Statistics I used, from 2006, were at the
height of the housing bubble. They show high growth in Las Vegas NV
and several Florida cities where houses are now worth half and income
growth is negative. One needs current statistics to assess places that
have changed since 2006. 

(Snipped quibble on power to avoid getting into Adlerian psychology.)
```

_(thread depth: 8)_

- **From:** Robert <no@email.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-10T14:18:57-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1hok861bu7i73s8edaubj5sr46s1s5tqem@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com> <b4df86ln15v15iglvsjb5g00tohco4slb4@4ax.com> <i6apfp$rbh$1@reader1.panix.com> <hraj869tr55757uf4pchto174p4merqnok@4ax.com> <i6d7fd$9fb$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
On Fri, 10 Sep 2010 12:14:38 +0000 (UTC), docdwarf@panix.com () wrote:

>In article <hraj869tr55757uf4pchto174p4merqnok@4ax.com>,
>Robert Wagner  <no@email.com> wrote:
…[28 more quoted lines elided]…
>that you are making guesses?

Blame the English Standards Workgroup (NL1.1 previously J-en), for
specifying the same verb form for present subjunctive and present
indicative, absent qualification, and for completely rejecting
epistemic verb forms. They expect us to indicate evidentality with
wimpy verb modifiers such as "I believe," "perhaps" and "apparently."
Worse, they ask us to indicate deductive modality with "may be" or
"must be." What nonsense, using "must," a verb meaning obligation, to
indicate uncertainty. 

Using such affectations would make us sound like cranky academecians.
Being a code cranker, I avoid pretentious language.
```

_(thread depth: 9)_

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2010-09-10T19:11:34+00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<i6dvt5$otq$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<fs76865ek3qm6gi1edgcme8l4utq1qc8io@4ax.com> <hraj869tr55757uf4pchto174p4merqnok@4ax.com> <i6d7fd$9fb$1@reader1.panix.com> <1hok861bu7i73s8edaubj5sr46s1s5tqem@4ax.com>`

```
In article <1hok861bu7i73s8edaubj5sr46s1s5tqem@4ax.com>,
Robert  <no@email.com> wrote:
>On Fri, 10 Sep 2010 12:14:38 +0000 (UTC), docdwarf@panix.com () wrote:
>
>>In article <hraj869tr55757uf4pchto174p4merqnok@4ax.com>,
>>Robert Wagner  <no@email.com> wrote:

[snip]

>>>I GUESSED Bridgeport is an economic satellite of NYC, but I did not
>>>guess at statistics showing it to be the best place to work in the US.
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>epistemic verb forms.

Leaving aside, by use of apophasis, how one might construct a subjunctive 
*without* qualification which would employ this case's verb form:

Bridgeport reflects - present indicative, 3rd pers. sing. verb

Bridgeport would reflect - subjunctive, 1st pers. sing. verb
Were Bridgeport to reflect - subjunctive, infinitive verb
Bridgeport possibly reflects - subjunctive(qualified), 3rd pers. sing. verb

... I am not trying to 'blame' anything, Mr Wagner; I asked if it was 
common for you to use an unqualified present-tense nominative indicative 
(ie, 'Bridgeport reflects NYC's statistics') to indicate that you are 
making guesses.

In attempting to assign a responsibility for this action it might seem 
that - for whatever reason - it is common for you to do so; knowing such 
might make it easier to evaluate your assertions (often unqualified 
present-tense nominative indicatives) in the future.

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL emulators

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-07T17:32:12-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<I3zho.128109$Bh.66425@en-nntp-12.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<70f04476-247e-4b83-ab4c-9ac0280dbdb1@l20g2000yqe.googlegroups.com>`

```
"RealInfo" <therightinfo@gmail.com> wrote in message 
news:70f04476-247e-4b83-ab4c-9ac0280dbdb1@l20g2000yqe.googlegroups.com...
> Hi all
> Is it possible to develop COBOL based applications on PC so that they
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Assuming you are aiming for IBM z/OS (those are the people who most often 
think "mainframe" is enough to say),

There are 3 (maybe 4) main vendors that provide full IBM mainframe 
development systems

 - IBM (see the RDz product)
 - Micro Focus (look for the Mainframe Express products)
 - Fujitsu (now Alchemy)
 - CA (I don't know if they are continuing develoment on their Realia 
products or not)

All of these products are VERY expensive for the "average" developer. 
However, they include JCL emulators, CICS, IMS, and DB2 options, Often 
IDCAMS and other utilities, etc.  In other words, they are true "IBM 
mainframe emulator environments". Many of these vendors also target the 
"port from the IBM mainframe to Windows or Unix/Linux" development tasks. 
In some cases, it is this "porting away from the mainframe" approach that is 
the primary buisness direction of the company.

If you simply want to develop (write, compile, and debug) COBOL on a PC, 
there are several otehr options.  Most of the other options have "IBM 
compatibiiity" options for syntax (and run-time behavior).  Some (not all) 
have EBCDIC support.  These other options range from "free" to inexpensive. 
However, they don't provide a "real" IBM mainframe type environment and 
often (usually?) don't stay current with new features and facilities 
available to IBM mainframe programmers.
```

#### ↳ Re: OT: JCL Emulators

- **From:** PR <paul.raulerson@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-14T13:39:00-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6b7e4012-fe4f-4782-832c-162ead697057@j2g2000vbo.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<bcb0280a-5058-459f-a57a-115f8a306c7a@i5g2000yqe.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Sep 8, 3:10 pm, Alistair <alist...@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> wrote:
> Being an IBMer; does anyone know of a free to private use JCL
> emulator? Ditto for CICS emulators...
>
> I expect a negative so anything non-Hercules based will be a positive.

If you are just wanting it to play with, you can load a copy of OS/2
in a VM, and pick up an old copy of IBM VisualAge COBOL off ebay.
Voila - instant CICS environment, including development. I wrote a LOT
of CICS code on that exact same setup. :)

Indeed, I had a customer still running it until November of last year,
with I think, 30 terminals. I moved them to a iSeries machine, and
ported all their custom code, but I sure loved that little CICS
environment.

-Paul
```

## Thread: OT: What Would You Do In This Situation? — 1 this month / 30 total

_Topics: [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

_Thread started [2010-08](2010-08.md#t-4736628e3e)._

#### ↳ Re: OT: What Would You Do In This Situation?

- **From:** Gilberto Strapazon <gilbertopb@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-08T14:50:45-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7b7de949-91ce-45c5-b0a7-bc5a9bab9018@t20g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<q8CdncXzgbuKL_DRnZ2dnUVZ_qydnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
On 19 ago, 19:37, "Charles Hottel" <chot...@earthlink.net> wrote:
> I am looking for more concrete options on how to handle the following
> situation.
>


A bit latter, but currently I have not come here frequently. Hope I
can add something.

Well, first of all, congrats for being asked for such project. Appears
to be an interesting oportunity, IMHO, if you can take it without
repent of course ;)
By myself, I love to work with this kind of system, there´s a lot to
learn and to to. Parsing, strings, extract information from some
strutured base like Cobol source code may be a good chalenge.

About the Access, appears you are a veteran too, so don´t mind to much
about. Ms-Access and VBA, IMHO, is a great development tool.
With Access, you can use wizards or just the main tools to easy and
fast create forms and reports that don´t require great dificult.
But, with the same Ms-Access, and using the VBA, then you can create
GREAT code. You have the Visual Basic APIs, so can do almost anything,
since using some of the most inner Windows resources to explore
inteligent graphics interfaces, or work with intrincated logic
routines, like the system you wrote about.

Also, you can use Ms-Access as a tool for development, together with
SQL Server, Oracle, DB2, and so on, thus having great stability and
secure processing.

I worked with Cobol for +20 years, some 10 with Acces, 17 with
Clipper, java and others, of course some times are mixed with others,
as I have only some +33 years on development ;)  In this years, I
found Access to be a very confortably tool. Currently I´m again with
Cobol (and Oracle), but this is my job, so I can´t choose all the
times ;)

About the project, I learned:
-No documentation? uhm... this means you have to reenginer all that or
just rewrite it all. Usually the second options is better.
-Some parts work? Evaluate clearly what is missing. Again, may be
desirable write all that again.
-The most important is: It´s clear what the system have to do? People
have clear on their minds and are able to give this info it to you?

You must know what you have to do, clearly. If people don´t know what
they want, nor how this would be, this is a dangerous alarm.

Don´t take scheduling time from what people say. YOU have to have
clear in your mind what you are going to do. Of course, we cant have
all in mind, as software development means a good intuition too, and
being able to have some idea on what is needed. Then, use the world
famous time calc formula: multiply the specifications by two or three.
Usually the time will become short (thanks to Murphy´s laws), but you
will be more confortably about it.

Be sure to be well paid in advance. Don´t expect to be paymment after
all processes. This include some (miraculous or so atraent) percent on
improvements someone will show being sooooo good. If it´s so good, and
serious, they can pay you now and the, after pay a good bonus,
including that famous percents... (LOL) You will be working for an
investnment of others, not the oposite.

Back to the system, I would love to do something so, hope you find
your mind in clear, have a good machine and nice room to work.
You will find very good sites with reference for Access and VBA that
will help you. Studying parsing, compiler construtions, etc, will be
really important and you will see that´s many things are developed and
well explained by many colleagues around the world.

Don´t forget to take time to yourself, yoru spirit, your family of
course.
Take a good breath and go!

Best Regards

Gilberto Strapazon
http://cwconnect.computerworld.com.br/zenta
```

```
Some info about the Windows side:

http://www-01.ibm.com/common/ssi/cgi-bin/ssialias?subtype=ca&infotype=an&appname=iSource&supplier=897&letternum=ENUS210-342

Hardware requirements
For COBOL for Windows, V7.6

  a.. Processor: Intel Pentium III 800 MHz (minimum) or compatible processor
  b.. 256 MB of memory (512 MB, or higher, recommended)
  c.. Disk space: 210 MB for COBOL compiler, tools, and product information
Software requirements
For application development and deployment, one of the following:

  a.. Microsoft Windows Server 2003 Standard or Enterprise Edition, SP1
  b.. Microsoft Windows Server 2008 Standard or Enterprise Edition
  c.. Microsoft Windows Server 2008 R2 Standard or Enterprise Edition
The program's specifications and specified operating environment information 
may be found in documentation accompanying the program, if available, such 
as a README file, or other information published by IBM, such as an 
announcement letter. Documentation and other program content may be supplied 
only in the English language.
```

<a id="t-d9721ea7c2"></a>
## Thread: [OT] Platform Stability in a Different World — 43 msgs

### [OT] Platform Stability in a Different World

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2010-09-16T18:58:41+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<i6tpd1$h35$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```

So... I was reading someplace else, got directed to 
<http://bucks.blogs.nytimes.com/2010/09/14/chases-online-banking-outage/?ref=business> 
and read:

--begin quoted text:

Potentially millions of Chase retail and small-business customers were 
frozen out of their online bank accounts for more than 24 hours because of 
a technical glitch, officials of the bank said.

[snip]

Chase, the retail banking arm of JPMorgan Chase, is the nations 
second-largest bank. More than 16.5 million of its customers have online 
accounts.

--end quoted text

... and then a guy posted about his experience dealing with Chase 
(permission to repost without attribution was given):

--begin quoted text:

I don't think we were impacted by their outage, but we've run up against 
their lousy app development practices time and again.

Way back when we were first rolling out W2k, we couldn't upgrade our 
treasurer's PC for nearly a year because the banking app we had to use 
wasn't compatible with W2k.

Recently, we've discovered their online apps frequently require the use of 
outdated (i.e., insecure) JVMs.  Upgrading to newer JVMs and removing the 
older JVMs requires some quasi-supported registry hacking.

And we have a check-deposit system that allows us to do the check scanning 
at our site.  But the web-based check-scanning app isn't yet compatible 
with Win7 at all, and they're only working on a version that works in 
32-bit Win7, not 64-bit.

--end quoted text

... and it got me to musing.  Recently there have been discussions about 
the Oldene Dayse, code that's old enough to vote and was last touched to 
take out the EXHIBIT NAMED statements during Y2K recompiles, sequestered 
programmers whose only glimpses of women were tke Keypunch Girls they were 
permitted to visit every other week with stacks of Hollerith cards...

... and then there's the above.  W2k (Windows 2000) came out a decade or 
so back and code that breaks because of an Operating Systems change is (as 
I was taught) the realm of Systems Jockies, not Applications Coders... and 
yet here's a fellow mentioning difficulties with folks relying on outdated 
Java Virtual Machines (outdated Java?) and check-scanning applications 
that have trouble not with the Operating System (Win7) but with the 
architecture (32- vs 64-bit) it runs on.

I am not advocating a return to the Oldene Dayse... but these are truly 
different times.  Twenty-five years ago or so a new-Standard compiler was 
introduced... but outside of that the 9-track tapes that the Payroll 
Office had been keeping (in accordance with The Law) since the early 1960s 
could (if the magnetic-particle-containing top coat wasn't peeling off the 
substrate) still be read and re-saved on more 'modern' media.

Twenty-five years ago or so IBM introduced the 96-tracks-per-inch 
5.25-inch floppy disk for the PC/AT and I remember marvelling at how over 
a meg o' stuff' could be stored on such a thing.  Were the Payroll Office 
to need the datasets... errrrr, files that were stored on such things now 
there'd be a hurdle or two to overcome.

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: [OT] Platform Stability in a Different World

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-09-17T13:27:01+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8ffuf6FetgU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<i6tpd1$h35$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> So... I was reading someplace else, got directed to
> <http://bucks.blogs.nytimes.com/2010/09/14/chases-online-banking-outage/?ref=business>
…[70 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD

Chase may not be a typical example. They have always struggled with IT and I 
endorse what the poster says.

Part of their problem is that they have always outsourced their IT to 
consultancies and not developed significant development expertise in house.

You can see their point. If you have virtually unlimited money it is 
tempting to simply buy a solution. The argument would be:"We are bankers, 
not computer people; as long as we buy the best available we should be fine 
and if there are problems we have the leverage to get them sorted."

It is a convincing argument.

I worked for them in London (when they were still "Chase Manhattan") in the 
mid 1970s.

They decided that they wanted a state-of-the-art Forex (Foreign Exchange) 
system so they retained Arthur Andersen to design it and IBM to provide the 
latest hardware for it.

I think I have described the ensuing fiasco here previously so I won't 
recap, but the main points were:

1. The Arthur Andersen consultant was incompetent.
2. IBM had not yet produced the hardware (3790) and it existed as a few 
prototype machines back in the States.
3. Nobody knew the 3790 Assembler.
4. Testing and debugging for it had to be done on a mainframe using an 
emulator.

Obviously, as it was a high profile project with a bottomlless pit of money 
attached, the pimps were on it like flies round a cowpat.

They wanted people who could learn Assembler overnight and "hit the ground 
running". Apparently I qualified and found myself pulled off another project 
and sent to join the prestigious "Front End Team". I was still a relatively 
new contractor and hadn't yet learned the ropes of contracting. (I was still 
trying to do my very best to deliver what was wanted...)

An Irishman and I very quickly realised that the system as designed could 
never work and the hardware could never handle it. He was more experienced 
at contracting than I was, and was using his contracting role to feed an 
expensive Raj Nish habit that required him to live with his partner and 
their baby in a London squat while he earnd about 5 times the national 
average, so they could go to Poona once a year and hand it all over to their 
guru.. I suggested we should raise an alarm and he said "No, say nothing. 
Just do the work and take the money for as long as it lasts...".   I wasn't 
having that, so I did some emulations and took them to the AA guy. He 
dismissed it as nonsense and told me to get on with it. I went to the IBM 
rep. and she at least had a look and agreed to do some more testing back at 
IBM.

(The transaction volumes for the system had never been estimated or 
investigated (Hooray for AA!) and the system simply didn't have enough 
registers or memory to support the task switching that would be required.)

IBM came back and said their tests had showed that the system as ordered 
couldn't handle the workload, so they upgraded it (at a special price.) We 
still never saw any hardware.

AA guy said I was a troublemaker (which was probably true) and I was fired. 
My pimp was very angry with me and told me I would never work in London 
again. (He was wrong.) I learned some valuable lessons.

A few months later I was having a beer with the Irishman in a pub and asked 
him how the implementation had gone. He said they didn't implement the 3790 
solution but went with DEC instead. He was still there and still raking it 
in...

When you look at this in terms of the original Management decision to buy 
the best, you can understand there must have been some wailing and gnashing 
of teeth at Chase. When the "best" isn't good enough, what do you do?

Nevertheless, they eventually got their system and they probably counted it 
as a success.

Although IT people may see inadequacy and inefficiency, the rest of the 
organisation only sees results.

"It's an IT problem. Man those guys are useless... takes them forever to get 
anything done and we never get what we need..." I'm sure you've heard the 
mantra...

Another very well known American Bank I worked for in London had a slightly 
different policy. They trained their own people into IT and made sure that 
if systems were outsourced they had an IT savvy person, hands on, who 
understood the Bank's requirements and could resolve design issues 
immediately. They were a pleasure to work with and I ended up doing several 
projects for them. It got to the point where we would discuss requirements, 
they would give me a budget and I'd recruit the necessary people and deliver 
it. I reported regularly  (informally on a daily basis, and formally once a 
week) to their liaison guy and if we had problems they would immediately do 
what was needed to resolve them.

Corporate culture has very much to do with success, in IT and everything 
else.

Pete
```

#### ↳ Re: Platform Stability in a Different World

- **From:** Alistair <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2010-09-17T08:11:36-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<993e433c-953d-4417-8b9c-4fac62d20722@f26g2000vbm.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<i6tpd1$h35$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```
On Sep 16, 7:58 pm, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
Platform stability? Intel have announced this week their new chipset
(destined to be unleashed upon the public in 2011 at earliest) which
they expect to replace the current outdated PC architecture. The one
improvement (?) is that the chipset will have on-board graphics
thereby making the drawing of screens a lot quicker. AMD (ahead of the
game) are having trouble with their chipset with on-board graphics. I
normally only upgrade my pc when the next generation game requires a
newer faster chip/graphics card/operating system) so it looks like we
will all be upgrading motherboards every two years or so in the
future. I wonder how long it will be before I mistakenly buy a Windows
7 only game and am forced to buy the OS to play it on?

Operating systems even within a vendor don't appear to be upwardly
compatible. Java has had problems with more modern versions not being
backwardly compatible (1.6 and 1.5 are not compatible just ask Gon
Higgins on the z390 Assembler project). On the internet it is
necessary for Javascript code-arounds to cater for incompatibility
between different browsers and different versions within a browser.

As for optical and magnetic media... I have read recommendations that
magnetic media (hard drives, floppies, tapes and drums (remember
those?)) and optical media (CDs and DVDs) be refreshed
 at regular intervals (10 years and two years respectively IIRC). It
looks like those Hollerith cards would outlast modern storage media
(unless you dropped them on the floor).
```

```
The problem is that no medium of data storage is entirely secure and
permanent. Magnetic media, at high packing densities, is subject to
deterioration due to external interferences such as cosmic rays. Even
punched cards will deteriorate with time.
```

```
That is true primarily for one specific vendor. For example in my
Apache logs I get:

MSIE 8.0; Windows NT 5.1; Trident/4.0; .NET CLR 1.1.4322; .NET CLR
2.0.50727; .NET CLR 3.0.4506.2152; .NET CLR 3.5.30729)

Why have they got 4 separate versions ? Because they are incompatible.
Apparently if you want to write an IE plugin you have to write
separate versions for each CLR if you want it to run 'everywhere'.

incompatible with 6.x and all prior versions and has completely
different development. The Silverlight isn't even compatible and it
won't run Silverlight in the browser at all.

"""I discovered that I can use the java javac options -target and -
source to compile the Java Applet on 1.6 and make it compatible with
1.4+ so it should work on any system with J2SE 1.4+ installed."""

Java is forwards compatible, but like every other language, is only
backwards compatible when requested.

It was Microsoft that broke Java compatability, MS's Java added stuff
and left out stuff so that programs would only run on Windows, that is
why Sun sued them and won (which led to Anders Hejlsberg, bought in
from Borland, to develop C#).

Meanwhile in Unix/Linux land ...

> On the internet it is
> necessary for Javascript code-arounds to cater for incompatibility
> between different browsers and different versions within a browser.

That is primarily IE. Mozilla developed Javascript and the DOM then MS
implemented an incompatible version. Each new version of IE failed to
be _forwards_ compatible so there are sites, especially intranets,
that are still locked to IE6.
```

```
will simply say: "I use Firefox." :-)

Steve, there's nothing wrong with Firefox (it's a very good browser) but so 
is IE.

I guess my irritation with this kind of argument stems from people being 
emotional about software and software vendors. I'm not on commission for 
Microsoft but I use their products without problem every day and make a 
living from it. They provide me with free tools which enable me to make 
money and they don't charge license fees (in fact they specifically offer 
Express versions so you can evaluate their tools for free) or runtime fees. 
I appreciate their support so I defend them in forums such as this one. But 
that doesn't mean I love or hate them, and I certainly don't believe their 
products are perfect. (Neither do they; in fact they spend sums that you and 
I could only dream of getting things right.)

In answer to my own question above, and as someone who has run every version 
of IE, I can categorically say: "Never."

As a web developer, I need to maintain at least a degree of Browser 
compatibility and have invested in (quite expensive) tools to ensure this 
(not from MS). But I still check all sites I build in both Firefox and IE. 
Invariably, they render correctly in both. If I should stray into MS only 
Javascript or HTML extensions, the tools I now use alert me, but I don't use 
Javascript very much any more, having learned that compiled server side code 
is more flexible and MUCH more secure. (Irrespective of the Browser).

For the average user, esoteric arguments about what is standard for web 
pages don't mean much. The only thing that matters is the user experience 
and this is more than adequate on both IE and Firefox.

While you may feel that Firefox is secure, I can assure you that NO software 
is secure against a determined  (and knowledgeable) attacker.

It is an illusion based on perception gleaned from reading stuff posted by 
journalists who have no idea about IT.

Pete.
```

```
the converse is true (in fact, I suspect it isn't). I used  client side 
Javascript  (with COBOL CGI and ISAPI) for a couple of years before I moved 
to C# and became quite a dab hand at writing Javascript and modifying other 
people's. Although it was fun, using the full facilities of C# and .NET on 
the server is much more fun.

a full programming facility available.
```

```
I am not sure what you were doing with Javascript that could be
replaced by a server code generating a static page, but it isn't what
Javascript is usually used for.

I use Javascript to pop up a calendar when users enter a date field,
to validate data fields as they enter, for autocompletion, to
highlight related data.  You can't do that on the server, not without
a page refresh (or AJAX which is Javascript anyway).

> I'm not sure that
> the converse is true (in fact, I suspect it isn't). I used  client side
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> the server is much more fun.

SpiderMonkey.

> C# and ASP.NET does it for me.
>
> AJAX means too many round trips and generated Javascript (for me... many
> people find it indispensible)

I am not sure how you think that full page refreshes are fewer round
trips. For example I have AJAX tables using JQuery. The table shows
10, or 20 items at a time. To get the next page is either a full page
refresh or an AJAX interaction to get just the data items. The
advantage is that the table is far more interactive with the user with
column sorts, searches and paging responding as the user selects
elements.

The point about AJAX is that it is asynchronous, data base validation
back to the server occurs as the user continues, for example, filling
a form.

> I keep meaning to get into Silverlight, but haven't done so yet. Adobe Flash
> meets my current requirements.
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…

They have a vested interest in selling you stuff. It is like getting
reports on the state of the hen house from the fox.

> from time to time. However, I do find Microsoft's releases a pleasant relief
> from the MS bashing that goes on here.

You sound just like a fanboi. You regard factual reports as 'MS
bashing'.

For example: what is 'MS bashing' and not 'fair comment' about saying
that Microsoft was the main cause of """On the internet it is
necessary for Javascript code-arounds to cater for incompatibility
between different browsers and different versions within a
browser."""

What is 'MS bashing' about """Operating systems even within a vendor
don't appear to be upwardly compatible.""" when it is necessary to
have four different versions of the .NET CLR (and thus of IE plugins)
for that very reason.

What is 'MS bashing' to point out in response also that the new
Windows Mobile 7 is completely incompatible, not only with WM6.x but
with current web based Silverlight even though the SDK is supposedly
Silverlight based.


> And I do understand they may be
> biased. But then, I apply that criterion to much of what I read from
> multifarious sources.
```

```
http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=fanboi

1. 	fanboi

Someone who is hopelessly devoted to something and will like anything
associated with thier particular thing.

That damn fanboi only likes that game cause Capcom made it.

The only reason he bought that car is cause he is a Japanese fanboi.

2. 	fanboi

Geek Term related to forum users who think a product/company/person
can do no wrong.

No matter many bugs Star Wars Galaxies has, a fanboi will alway defend
the developers.
```

```
On Mon, 20 Sep 2010 13:07:22 +1200, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

>I guess my irritation with this kind of argument stems from people being 
>emotional about software and software vendors.

People tend to like or dislike Microsoft and Apple products because
they are Microsoft or Apple products.   Apparently the label is
important and many consumers define themselves by their choices.

In the case of IE though I do have a problem with a product called
BlueZone.   BlueZone is a terminal program emulating IBM mainframe
terminals such as the 3270.    When we go to a local site, it checks
to see if we are exceeding our license and (I think downloads) the
current version of the program.   It also creates a desktop icon so
that contains the bookmark.

When we first got it, it only ran in I.E. using Active-X.    Later on,
it could run on Java instead, but the web page we started off on just
checked to see if we are using I.E., if so, it went to an Active-X
page to log on, otherwise it went to a Java page to log on.    I have
no idea why it did this, as I.E. can run BlueZone from the Java page.
At any rate, the icon on the desktop remembers which way we started
BlueZone and won't check the browser.   I like to have a clean desktop
anyway, and I don't want to have the icon think I'm using I.E. because
that's the last way I started BlueZone - even if my default browser is
Opera or Firefox or Safari or Chrome or whatever.

With our new tougher security, machines running Windows 7 can't run
BlueZone at all using I.E., so they have to use a different browser.

BlueZone isn't the only program that has problems with different
browsers.    (It may be the only one I use for CoBOL though!!)

But most of the web pages that were designed for the de facto browser
I.E. have been updated for de jure rules - and I.E. has been updated
to fit them better as well.
```

<a id="t-247153f7fe"></a>
## Thread: Not (intended to be) a "Commercial" — 31 this month / 33 total

### Not (intended to be) a "Commercial"

- **From:** "Bill Klein" <wmklein@noreply.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2010-09-16T22:24:22-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<GbBko.157427$Is6.93397@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
I have recently downloaded the free trial of the new Visual COBOL R2 from 
Micro Focus. Today, I watched their "kick-off" video at:

http://vs2010.microfocus.com/visual-cobol.htm


clicking on the

"Watch the launch webcast"


link. I had to give personal information (that others may not want to do), 
but I was pretty impressed with this product (at least the online demo).


It does seem to do an excellent job of providing "state of the art" 
development along with supporting both 'traditional" and "new" style COBOL.


I am NOT saying that the prices of this product (or deployment of the object 
code that it creates) will meet the needs of many participants in this 
newsgroup, but as a "show place" of where and how COBOL can be integrated 
into a .NET (now, and Unix, Linux later) environments seems like a goal that 
other commercial and non-commercial COBOL implementations could aim for.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Not (intended to be) a "Commercial"

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-09-18T04:33:33+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8fhjj0Fu7rU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<GbBko.157427$Is6.93397@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com> <alBko.161961$mN7.105974@en-nntp-08.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Bill Klein wrote:
> I messed up the URL in my original post.  (It needs an "l' at the
> end.  It should be
…[30 more quoted lines elided]…
>> non-commercial COBOL implementations could aim for.

OK, that link works, but I can't see a video unless I download a trial of 
the product and I really don't want to do that.

Reading the new features it would seem that the major advance is providing 
Visual Studio as the IDE. That is certainly a Good Thing.

Why can't I get excited about having SQL in COBOL? Because it's already 
obsolete.

LINQ (and Lamdas repesenting complex queries) is light years ahead of it.

Still, it would be nice to be able to manipulate result sets in COBOL and it 
looks like this supports that.

XML in COBOL?  Had it for years.

From the "Features" and "Benefits" it looks "good" but nothing to get 
excited about. These are facilities that COBOL has been crying out for for 
years. The other languages have had them for years. (And more).

I would say it is a good implementation of COBOL. It is still playing "catch 
up" with C# and VB.Net as far as .Net development goes...

Pete.
```

```
wanting to do that.

If you click on the "watch launch" location, what message do you get?
```

#### ↳ Re: Not (intended to be) a "Commercial"

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2010-09-18T04:17:39+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8fhil7FohoU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<GbBko.157427$Is6.93397@en-nntp-13.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
Bill Klein wrote:
> I have recently downloaded the free trial of the new Visual COBOL R2
> from Micro Focus. Today, I watched their "kick-off" video at:
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
> implementations could aim for.

Come on, Bill. They ALL integrate easily, PROVIDED you write Object Classes, 
or wrap your existing legacy code as an Object Class.

The provided link gives a 404 (page not found) when I access it.

You might not be aware that existing COBOL runs perfectly well under .NET 
using the InterOP services which MS provided for legacy code as part of the 
.NET framework.

I've been running Fujitsu NetCOBOL  in .NET for several years  now, without 
any problem whatsoever. The COBOL code integrates with .NET code (C# and 
VB.NET) completely seamlessly.

The only reason I  can see why anyone would buy a very expensive CLR 
generating COBOL compiler is so they can run their COBOL as managed code. It 
runs slower than unmanaged code (which is native) and provides no advantage 
whatsoever apart from the psychological one of it being managed.

(Basically, this means that the framework will close it down properly if it 
misbehaves (primarily addressing exceptions). If code is properly debugged 
and has been running in Production for some time without subscripts going 
out of range, the risk is low. (Actually, if you're really worried about 
exceptions being caught and handled properly, you can specify TRY... CATCH 
blocks for unmanaged code just like you can for managed code (as long as you 
are using InterOP services.))

It doesn't get you away from dependency on COBOL and simply perpetuates the 
use of it, in an environment that COBOL is not well suited for.

I can't see a case for managed COBOL.

After a year or two the programmers realize it takes them far too long to do 
stuff in COBOL which they could do in a fraction of the time with .Net 
languages, and the management realize that these languages are free, so they 
have an expensive white elephant sitting on their hands.

Anybody moving to .NET will eventually move off COBOL, so why would you buy 
an expensive compiler for a language you are trying to get away from?

The usual answer is that people are told to buy the compiler, and don't 
understand the .Net environment or the facilities available in it, so they 
do.  (Or maybe they know .Net but don't know COBOL so they take the advice 
on that which they are given.)

Then they find there are no credits or refunds... I've had people actually 
offer me  NetCOBOL for .NET as a gift. (A legal transfer of licence, when 
they found they didn't need it and couldn't get a credit from Alchemy). I 
turned it down. No need or use for it. Ironic really. A few years back I was 
desperately trying to buy it, because, like everybody else, I thought it was 
necessary.

I have a free Ferrari in the garage. Why would I drive a model T with a 
Ferrari engine, but no equivalent ABS, stability, suspension, or 
accessories, for which I paid a large sum of money, just because I was used 
to driving a model T? It's far easier (and much more rewarding) to learn to 
drive the Ferrari...

Pete.
```

```
Bill Klein wrote:
> Pete,
>   Just to make it clear, the things tha I most liked about the product
> (from the video) were development tools and not whether it provided
> managed or non-managed support (as it supports both).  I do hope that
> you are able to view the video and see how it works.

I clicked on "view the video" and all I got was a background animation of 
some dishes going through an oven.

I saw that it supports both managed and non-managed code from the 
description. However, that is a normal feature of the Visual Studio 
environment and, while it may be new for COBOL, .Net developers have been 
enjoying it since 2003. (VS 2005 provided full integration of InterOP 
services, replacing the earlier  "pinvoke" (platform invoke) which was 
required. In 2008 MS released a P/Invoke tool which automatically converts 
unmanaged legacy to managed code. I have never used it but I hear it works 
very well. Few people are still using pinvoke.
>
> This does NOT mean that I  exepct you (or anyone else) to think that
> "COBOL is *the* best languge for .NET".  It is intended to say that I
> think that MF provides an excellent developmen environment (with this
> product) for doing COBOL development for .NET.

Fair enough. I would agree that Visual Studio is an amazing platform for 
.Net development and I would expect nothing less than excellence from Micro 
Focus, as a company.


> It certainly is
> better (IMHO) than any development IDE that I ever saw from Fujitsu
> (or Alchamy)

That is probably not fair, Bill. When they (Fujitsu) released NetCOBOL for 
.Net it came with Visual Studio (replacing the previous adequate, but blunt, 
COBOL IDE.)  I think Fujitsu would be the first to admit that their old 
COBOL IDE was simply not up to what was required for .Net. (And it looked 
laughable alongside VS...) They really had two choices:

1. Offer Eclipse as a tailored .Net IDE for COBOL
2. Offer a plugin to Visual Studio allowing COBOL as a language

I'm not sure (because, in the end I never bought the product) but I believe 
there was an option to have Eclipse (Open Source, I think...) or VS 
(Microsoft). Both of these platform IDEs are excellent. I have managed teams 
using Eclipse for Java development and I use VS myself with C# for .Net 
development. Both platforms are outstanding. Obviously, I have a preference 
for VS, but that has more to do with familiarity than any innate 
superiority.

I started out with the free version of Visual Studio (Express) and was so 
impressed with it that I bought the full Professional version. (It cost 
about quarter of the price for the .Net COBOL compiler.) It didn't add 
significant capability to the free version , (which is perfectly adequate 
for normal development) but it did provide some better extended interfaces 
and options for things which I might want to look at later. I'm currently 
running VS 2008 but expect to upgrade to VS 2010 around the same time as I 
change development to specifically target windows 7 and/or mobile devices.

I suspect that some of the things which may have "impressed" you in the 
presentation from MF may have more to do with VS than with COBOL. It is a 
very impressive piece of software and you start to wonder how you ever got 
by without it. It supports direct connection to RDB by a number of methods 
(Fujitsu only permits ODBC unless you use ActiveX to call ADO or create your 
own wrappers), complete integration of SQL and debugging it, seamless 
plugins that add reporting like Crystal and Stimulsoft directly to the IDE, 
ability to collapse and expand "regions" of code, book marks in code, search 
and replace that is a delight (and includes optional use of regular 
expressions) and allows you to search all files in a project (including ones 
you don't have open, if you want), full contextual help for the language in 
use (Intellisense), ability to add all kinds of resources (including COM and 
ActiveX, as well as scripts, templates, text, images, etc.) to your project 
and immediately have them integrated with Intellisense so you can see their 
method signatures, events, and properties in the contexts where you use 
them. The debugging facilities are simply amazing (I always thought Micro 
Focus Animator was one of the best pieces of software ever written, but VS 
debugging is better...) This is by no means a comprehensive list. Simply 
put, it is a developer's delight.

I don't have any problem with giving my details or registering for stuff. I 
have nothing to hide and have posted here (and other places on the web) for 
decades without using a pseudonym.

Pete.
```
